                <div class="date-outer">
                 <h2 class="date-header">
                  <span>
                   Sunday, 10 March 2013
                  </span>
                 </h2>
                 <div class="date-posts">
                  <div class="post-outer">
                   <div class="post hentry" itemprop="blogPost" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting">
                    <meta content="http://www.blogscanada.ca/wp-content/uploads/2013/03/images7-180x113.jpg" itemprop="image_url"/>
                    <meta content="5004857310426765016" itemprop="blogId"/>
                    <meta content="5028812230777266941" itemprop="postId"/>
                    <a name="5028812230777266941">
                    </a>
                    <h3 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name">
                     Huge asteroid whizzes past us again.
                    </h3>
                    <div class="post-header">
                     <div class="post-header-line-1">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-5028812230777266941" itemprop="description articleBody">
                     <div class="cat-bar">
                      <div class="ribbon left">
                       <div class="ribbon-inner">
                        <div class="left-wrapper">
                         <div class="cat-name">
                          <a class="darken tooltip cboxElement" href="http://www.blogscanada.ca/wp-content/uploads/2013/03/images7.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;">
                           <img alt="images" class="attachment-single-small wp-post-image" height="113" src="http://www.blogscanada.ca/wp-content/uploads/2013/03/images7-180x113.jpg" width="180"/>
                          </a>
                          Dear Readers:
                         </div>
                        </div>
                       </div>
                      </div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="post-content">
                      <div class="post-751098 post type-post status-publish format-standard hentry category-defence category-perspective-on-canada category-space tag-spotlight" id="post-751098">
                       Your faithful reporter doesnt know whats going on, but it seems like weve been in a shooting gallery lately!
                       <br/>
                       An asteroid as big as a city block shot relatively close by the Earth
 on Saturday, the latest in a series of visiting celestial objects 
including an asteroid the size of a bus that exploded over Russia last 
month, injuring 1,500.
                       <br/>
                       <em>
                        Discovered just six days ago, the 460-foot long (140-meter) 
Asteroid 2013 ET passed about 600,000 miles from Earth at 3:30 p.m. EST.
 Thats about 2-1/2 times as far as the moon, fairly close on a cosmic 
yardstick.
                       </em>
                       <br/>
                       <div id="yui_3_5_1_22_1362960376104_223">
                        <em>
                         The scary part
 of this one is that its something we didnt even know about, Patrick 
Paolucci, president of Slooh Space Camera, said during a webcast 
featuring live images of the asteroid from a telescope in the Canary 
Islands.
                        </em>
                       </div>
                       <em>
                        Moving at a speed of about 26,000 miles per hour, 
the asteroid could have wiped out a large city if it had impacted the 
Earth, added Slooh telescope engineer Paul Cox.
                       </em>
                       <br/>
                       <div id="yui_3_5_1_22_1362960376104_225">
                        <em>
                         Asteroid 2013 
ET is nearly eight times larger than the bus-sized asteroid that 
exploded over Chelyabinsk, Russia, on February 15. The force of the 
explosion, equivalent to about 440 kilotons of dynamite, created a shock
 wave that shattered windows and damaged buildings, injuring more than 
1,5000 people.
                        </em>
                       </div>
                       <em>
                        Later that day, another small asteroid, known as 
DA14, passed about 17,200 miles from Earth, closer than the orbiting 
networks of communications and weather satellites.
                       </em>
                       <br/>
                       <em>
                        One of the reasons why were finding more of these objects is that there are more people looking, Cox said.
                       </em>
                       <br/>
                       <div id="yui_3_5_1_22_1362960376104_224">
                        <em>
                         Two other small
 asteroids, both about the size of the Russian meteor, will also be in 
Earths neighborhood this weekend. Asteroid 2013 EC 20 passed just 
93,000 miles away on Saturday  a stones thrown, said Cox.
                        </em>
                       </div>
                       <em>
                        On Sunday, Asteroid 2013 EN 20 will fly about 
279,000 miles from Earth. Both were discovered just three days ago. We 
know that the solar system is a busy place, said Cox.
                       </em>
                       <br/>
                       <em>
                        Were not sitting here on our pale, blue dot on 
our own in nice safety  This should be a wakeup call to governments.
                       </em>
                       <br/>
                       <em>
                        NASA has been tasked by the U.S. Congress to find 
and track all near-Earth objects 0.62 miles or larger in diameter, and 
estimates about 95 percent have been identified.
                       </em>
                       <br/>
                       <em>
                        However, only about 10 percent of smaller asteroids have been discovered, NASA scientists have said.
                       </em>
                       <br/>
                       <em>
                        The effort is intended to give scientists and 
engineers as much time as possible to learn if an asteroid or comet is 
on a collision course with Earth, in hopes of sending up a spacecraft or
 taking other measures to avert catastrophe.
                       </em>
                       <br/>
                       <a href="http://news.yahoo.com/earth-gets-rush-weekend-asteroid-visitors-001945056.html">
                        http://news.yahoo.com/earth-gets-rush-weekend-asteroid-visitors-001945056.html
                       </a>
                       <br/>
                       About 100 tons of material from space hitus every day
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                     </div>
                     <div style="clear: both;">
                     </div>
                    </div>
